## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t). The nonlinearity appears in the position-dependent restoring force.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring + linear damping)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (anharmonic restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing oscillator with damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Duffing oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonically driven with damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect symmetric potentials in physical oscillators
- Even-power terms (x**2) in restoring force break spatial symmetry — indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v indicate viscous/linear damping; terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v indicate self-excited oscillations (limit cycles)
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving — look for resonance phenomena
- Products of x**2 * v suggest amplitude-dependent damping where energy dissipation rate depends on displacement
- Absence of time t as an explicit variable suggests an autonomous system — phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Rational restoring forces like x/(1+c*x**2) model bounded/saturating spring forces at large displacements
- Sign of cubic coefficient relative to linear term determines hardening (same sign as linear) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior

I need to determine which candidates can match the GT: `F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v` = `0.7675*sin(t) - 0.2639*v*sin(x)`.

Key observation: The GT has two terms:
1. `F0*sin(t)` — a pure sine of t
2. `-beta*v*sin(x)` — v times sine of x

Note that `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, and `-v*sin(x) = v*cos(x + π/2)`. These identities will be useful.

**GT: 0.767518260471059·sin(t) - 0.263896435020576·v·sin(x)**

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The GT has two terms:
1. A sin(t) term (which equals cos(t - π/2))
2. A -v·sin(x) term (which equals v·cos(x + π/2))

**Key identities:**
- sin(t) = cos(t - π/2) = cos(π/2 - t)
- -v·sin(x) = v·cos(x + π/2)
- sin(t) = sin(1·t + 0)
